## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the right-hand side of a population dynamics ODE. The presence of both P and t suggests possible time-varying growth parameters, carrying capacity, or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with critical minimum population)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (per-capita growth rate increases then decreases with density)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P * sin(c3 * t) (logistic with seasonal forcing)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (logistic growth with proportional harvesting)
- Constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant yield harvesting)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth model)
- Time-dependent growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (linearly changing intrinsic growth rate)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (time-decaying Malthusian parameter)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth minus linear death)
- von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic-catabolic balance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt ~ c*P) → exponential/Malthusian growth regime, no density dependence
- Quadratic term in P (dP_dt ~ c0*P - c1*P**2) → logistic-type density-dependent regulation with carrying capacity
- Cubic polynomial in P (dP_dt ~ c0*P + c1*P**2 + c2*P**3) → Allee effect or bistability in population dynamics
- P*log(P) terms → Gompertz-type growth, often seen in biological growth with multiplicative stochasticity
- Trigonometric functions of t multiplied by P → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth
- Fractional powers of P (P**c with 0<c<1) → sub-linear growth, resource limitation at individual level
- Ratio P/(1+c*P) structure → contest competition or interference effects in per-capita resource acquisition
- Exponential functions of t → non-stationary environment with systematically changing conditions
- Product t*P → growth rate that scales with both population and elapsed time (e.g., learning, adaptation)
- dP_dt vanishing at specific P values → equilibrium points; number of real roots indicates number of steady states
